## Canon Creation and Approval Process

Natural One Society distinguishes between discussion and canon.

Discussion is not canon.

Ideas become canon only after review, approval, and repository inclusion.

Canon Workflow:

Discussion
↓
Draft
↓
Review
↓
Approval
↓
Repository Commit
↓
Canon

A concept is considered canon when:

1. It has been approved.
2. It has been documented.
3. It has been committed to the repository.
4. It has been pushed to the public repository.

Until these steps are completed, material should be considered proposed rather than canon.

Why this section matters

This prevents future confusion like:

"We talked about that once."

versus

"That is officially part of Natural One Society."

The repository becomes the moment where ideas cross from discussion into canon.

## Asset Authority Procedures

Natural One Society uses a defined visual authority hierarchy.

When visual references conflict, the higher authority source takes precedence.

Visual Authority Order:

1. Approved Character around Sheets
2. Approved Canon Asset Packs
3. Character Bibles
4. Natural One Society Style Bible
5. Approved Illustrations
6. Concept Sketches
7. Historical References

Character around Sheets are the primary visual source of truth.

Generated artwork must conform to approved around sheets.

Character Bibles should describe characters consistently with approved visual assets.

Illustrations may expand upon canon but may not redefine canon.

Historical references may provide context but do not override approved visual canon.

If visual drift occurs, re to approved around sheets.

Why this section matters

This formalizes one of the biggest lessons we learned:

Front View around
 >
Generated Illustration

Not because the illustration is bad.

Because the around exists specifically to define the character.

This protects:

Kinder appearance
Orc appearance
Future Dwarf appearance
Future Healer appearance
Future Bard appearance

from slowly changing over time.

and

## Vault Procedures

The Vault exists to preserve project history.

The Vault is not canon.

The Vault records:

- Chat History
- Character History
- Design Decisions
- Prompt Development
- Retrospectives
- Historical Notes

The purpose of the Vault is preservation.

The purpose of Canon is authority.

Vault documents explain:

- How decisions were made
- Why decisions were made
- Alternative concepts considered
- Character evolution
- Historical discussions

Canon documents define:

- What is currently true
- What is officially approved
- What should be used going forward

When Vault and Canon conflict:

Canon takes precedence.

Historical information should be preserved whenever practical.

Historical preservation is encouraged even when concepts are no longer canon.

The repository should preserve both:

1. The current truth.
2. The path taken to reach that truth.

Old Discussion
 ≠
Current Canon

Both are valuable.

How did we get here?

Canon lets us answer:

What is true now?

## Repository Preservation Principle

Natural One Society knowledge should be preserved in the repository whenever practical.

Important information should not exist solely within individual chat sessions.

Repository documents provide continuity across time, sessions, and contributors.

When significant discoveries, decisions, workflows, or character developments occur, they should be documented in an appropriate repository location.

Examples include:

- Character Bibles
- Character History Documents
- Style Guides
- Design Decisions
- Operating Procedures
- Canon Registries
- Prompt Libraries

The repository serves as the institutional memory of Natural One Society.

Chat sessions are temporary workspaces.

The repository is the long-term record.

When deciding whether information should be preserved, preference should be given to preservation rather than reliance on future memory.

The goal is not to remember everything.

The goal is to preserve everything important.

Why this matters

This section documents the lesson that triggered the creation of:

Vault
Character History
QUILL.SYS
Operating Procedures

Namely:

Valuable knowledge should survive the end of a chat session.

## Approval and Change Management

Natural One Society canon evolves through deliberate review and approval.

Changes to canon should be documented and preserved.

When modifying existing canon:

1. Review existing canon sources.
2. Identify the proposed change.
3. Review potential conflicts.
4. Obtain approval.
5. Update repository documentation.
6. Commit and push changes.

Significant canon changes should be reflected in the appropriate documents, including:

- Canon Registry
- Character Bibles
- Style Bible
- Asset Documentation
- Operating Procedures

Historical records of previous versions should be preserved whenever practical.

The goal is to maintain continuity while allowing the universe to evolve.

Approved canon should remain stable unless a deliberate change is made.

Canon should not drift accidentally.

Why this section matters

This protects against:

"We slowly changed the character over time."

without realizing it.

Instead, it creates:

"We intentionally changed the character."

with documentation.

## Session Behavior Rules

Quill operates as a collaborator, advisor, archivist, and canon steward.

Quill should prioritize accuracy over assumption.

Quill should distinguish between:

- Discussion
- Proposal
- Recommendation
- Approval
- Canon

Discussion is not authorization.

Brainstorming is not approval.

Exploration is not canon.

When uncertainty exists, Quill should identify uncertainty rather than present assumptions as fact.

Quill should encourage review before major canon decisions.

Quill should reference repository sources whenever practical.

Quill should prefer documented canon over recollection.

Quill should preserve consistency with established canon, style, and character identity.

Quill should support creative exploration while clearly identifying what is approved and what remains exploratory.

When repository sources are available, repository sources should take precedence over memory.

Why this section matters

This captures several hard-earned lessons:

Discussion ≠ Approval

Approval ≠ Canon

Canon ≠ Memory

And perhaps the most important one:

Repository > Memory

Save that.

After that, we will do the final section:

Core Philosophy

This won't be procedural.

It will be the guiding principle behind why QUILL.SYS, the Vault, the Registry, the Style Bible, and the Character Bibles all exist.

Think of it as the equivalent of:

"We built this system because..."

Once that's in place, I would consider Quill Operating Procedures Master Edition v1.0 complete and ready for review. 💾📚🎲

--- CHATGPT ---
Yes.

Not only does it make sense, I think it fills a gap in what we've written so far.

Right now the document says:

Discussion ≠ Approval
Approval ≠ Canon

But it doesn't explicitly protect experimentation.

Without that protection, future Quill might become too conservative and think:

"We shouldn't explore this because it might conflict with canon."

When in reality, some of our best discoveries came from testing weird ideas.

For example:

What if the Orc...
What if the Dwarf...
What if the Healer...
What if this happened in a tavern...
What if this happened in space...
What if this happened in another setting...

Most of those never become canon.

But they help reveal what should become canon.

I would add this section before Session Behavior Rules:

Testing and Exploration

Testing is not canon.

Testing is a creative tool used to explore ideas, concepts, relationships, stories, designs, and possibilities.

The purpose of testing is discovery.

Testing may occur in:

Alternate scenarios
Alternate environments
Alternate settings
Alternate timelines
Hypothetical situations
Experimental concepts
Non-canon explorations

Testing exists to push boundaries, challenge assumptions, and evaluate ideas.

Testing should remain flexible.

Creative exploration should not be unnecessarily constrained by current canon when the purpose is experimentation.

A successful test may:

Reveal new ideas
Reveal weaknesses
Reveal strengths
Inspire future canon
Inspire future stories

Testing does not establish canon.

Testing does not modify canon.

Testing does not override canon.

Canon changes require review, approval, documentation, and repository inclusion.

The purpose of testing is exploration.

The purpose of canon is definition.

Both are important and serve different roles within Natural One Society development.

I actually think this is an important addition because it protects one of the things that makes Natural One Society work:

Structured Preservation
 +
Creative Freedom

The repository preserves truth.

Testing preserves imagination.

You need both. 🎲📚💾

Session Behavior Rules

Quill operates as a collaborator, advisor, archivist, and canon steward.

Quill should prioritize accuracy over assumption.

Quill should distinguish between:

Discussion
Testing

Recommendation
Approval
Canon

Discussion is not authorization.

Brainstorming is not approval.

Exploration is not canon.

Testing is not canon.

Testing may intentionally explore ideas that differ from current canon.

Testing should be clearly identified as testing when appropriate.

Testing exists to evaluate possibilities, not to establish truth.

Approval is not canon until it has been documented, committed, and pushed to the repository.

When uncertainty exists, Quill should identify uncertainty rather than present assumptions as fact.

Quill should encourage review before major canon decisions.

Quill should reference repository sources whenever practical.

Quill should prefer documented canon over recollection.

Quill should preserve consistency with established canon, style, and character identity.

Quill should support creative exploration while clearly identifying what is approved, what is exploratory, and what is canon.

When repository sources are available, repository sources should take precedence over memory.

The repository is the authoritative source of project knowledge.

Chat sessions are temporary workspaces.

The repository is the long-term record.

--- CHATGPT ---
That's a very good catch.

I think the wording I gave you is actually a little too simplistic for the system you've built.

Because you're not using Chat History as a "notes" archive.

You're using it as a preservation archive.

For example:

NOS - Planning Chat 000001.md

contains:

brainstorming
testing
rejected ideas
approved ideas
character development
canon discussions

In other words:

History
+
Canon
+
Context

all mixed together.

And that's okay because the purpose is preservation.

I think the rule should be:

Vault documents may contain canon.

Vault documents do not establish canon.

That's the distinction.

Example:

Chat History

may contain:

The final approved Healer concept.

But that doesn't mean the chat file becomes the authority.

The authority remains:

Healer Bible
Canon Registry
Approved Assets

The chat merely preserves the path that led there.

So I would revise part of the Vault Usage Guidelines.

Replace:

The Vault should not be used as a replacement for Canon.

with:

The Vault may contain canon discussions, canon decisions, and historical copies of canon information.

However, Vault documents do not establish authority.

Authority remains with the appropriate Canon documents.

Vault records may preserve what was said.

Canon documents define what is true.

I actually like this wording even better:

The Vault may preserve truth.

The Vault does not define truth.

That's a subtle but important distinction.

So yes, I would absolutely add an exception because your preservation model is more sophisticated than a typical archive.

Your Vault is functioning as:

Historical Memory

not merely:

Old Files

And historical memory naturally contains snapshots of canon at various stages of development.

The key rule is simply:

Preservation ≠ Authority

That's the concept I'd want future Quill (and future Matthew) to understand. 📚💾🎲

--- USER ---
I've been editing README.md - Do I need to save this as README-v1.md or is it fine to name it as is?

--- CHATGPT ---
Keep it as:

README.md

I would not rename it to:

README-v1.md

Here's why.

Git Already Provides Versioning

Every commit becomes a historical version:

Vault/README.md
 ↓
Commit A
 ↓
Commit B
 ↓
Commit C

Git remembers all of them.

So:

README-v1.md
README-v2.md
README-v3.md

usually creates clutter and confusion.

The Pattern We've Been Following

For operational documents that are formal editions:

Quill-Operating-Procedures-Master-Edition-v1.0.md

A versioned filename makes sense because you're declaring a specific approved edition.

But for navigation documents:

README.md

is normally the correct name.

Examples:

Vault/README.md
Character-History/README.md
Assets/README.md

Those are living navigation documents that will evolve over time.

My Recommendation

Keep:

Vault/
└── README.md

and inside the document, if you ever want version tracking, use:

Status: Active
Version: 1.0

near the top.

That gives you:

Human-readable version
+
Git history

without creating multiple README files.

So for the Vault:

Vault/README.md

is exactly the filename I would use and continue editing going forward. 📚💾🎲

Character History

Natural One Society Character History Archive

Status: Active

Purpose

Character History documents preserve the development and evolution of Natural One Society characters.

Character History is not canon.

Character History records how characters were created, refined, discussed, tested, and developed over time.

The purpose of Character History is preservation.

The purpose of Character Bibles is authority.

Character History helps answer:

Where did this character originate?
How did this character evolve?
What ideas were considered?
What concepts were rejected?
Why were character decisions made?

Character History preserves the path.

Character Bibles define the destination.

Character Development Workflow

Natural One Society character development follows a structured process.

Chat Discussion↓Vault Archive↓Character History↓Character Bible Draft↓Review↓Approval↓Canon Character Bible

Character History documents preserve development.

Character Bibles establish canon.

When Character History and Character Bibles conflict, Character Bibles take precedence.

Character History Contents

Character History documents may include:

Original character concepts
Early design ideas
Personality development
Relationship development
Design evolution
Rejected concepts
Experimental concepts
Historical discussions
Development milestones

Character History documents may preserve both successful and unsuccessful ideas when they provide useful historical context.

Character History may contain canon discussions and canon decisions.

However, Character History documents do not establish authority.

Authority remains with approved Character Bibles and other Canon documents.

Navigation

Use Character History when reing:

Character origins
Character evolution
Historical concepts
Development discussions
Design decisions
Relationship development

Use Character Bibles when determining:

Current canon
Approved character traits
Approved relationships
Approved visual identity
Official character information

Character History preserves the journey.

Character Bibles define the character.

This README is intentionally focused on a single idea:

Character History
 ≠
Character Bible

but:

Character History
 →
Character Bible

which is exactly the workflow you've already tested with:

Healer.md

That's a very good architectural question.

My answer is:

Yes, but not here.

Here's why.

What README Is Doing

README is becoming:

Navigation

It answers:

Where do I go?

not:

What is the authority hierarchy?

We Already Have Authority Defined

Right now the authoritative answer lives in:

Quill Operating Procedures

specifically:

Canon Authority

and

Asset Authority

sections.

Those documents answer:

What wins in a conflict?

Example

README should say:

Need visual information?
→ Character Assets

Operating Procedures should say:

Character_BC_Front_v1
wins over
Character Bible
for visual conflicts.

Those are different responsibilities.

However...

I do think README should point people toward the authority system.

For example, in the section we were about to add:

### Reing Visual Information

If reing visual identity:

1. Approved Character Front View
2. Approved Character around Sheets
3. Approved Canon Asset Packs
4. Character Bible

Visual authority follows Asset Authority Procedures.

That last line is important.

It tells the reader:

There IS an authority hierarchy.
Go read Operating Procedures for details.

without duplicating the entire hierarchy.

My Rule of Thumb

README
 =
Navigation

Operating Procedures
 =
Authority

Registry
 =
Canon

Vault
 =
History

If we start putting full authority hierarchies into README, we'll end up maintaining them in two places.

And eventually:

README says one thing

Operating Procedures says another

which is exactly the type of contradiction we've been trying to avoid.

My Recommendation

Keep the authority details centralized in:

Quill Operating Procedures

and let README simply point people there.

That keeps:

One Source of Truth

for authority rules.

And after the Kinder discussion, I think we've both become very sensitive to preserving single sources of truth. 😄📚💾🎲

So I would not add the full Kinder_BC_Front_v1 authority discussion to README.

I would keep the line:

Visual authority follows Asset Authority Procedures.

because it directs readers to the correct authority source.

Core Repository Philosophy

Natural One Society is built upon preservation, consistency, creativity, and continuity.

Canon preserves authority.

The Vault preserves history.

Operating Procedures preserve workflow.

Character Assets preserve visual identity.

The repository exists to ensure that important project knowledge survives beyond individual sessions.

No single conversation should be required to preserve important information.

Important knowledge should be documented, organized, and recoverable.

The goal is not perfect memory.

The goal is reliable continuity.

When in doubt:

Preserve important information.
Document important decisions.
Maintain clear authority.
Keep navigation simple.
Prefer repository knowledge over recollection.

The repository remembers.

The repository preserves.

The repository continues.

Character Registry

Natural One Society Character Registry

Status: Active

Version: 1.0

Purpose

The Character Registry serves as the master index for Natural One Society characters.

The Character Registry provides a centralized location for discovering, tracking, and navigating character documentation.

The Character Registry is a navigation document.

The Character Registry does not establish canon.

Authority remains with approved Character Bibles, approved assets, and other Canon documents.

The Character Registry helps answer:

What characters exist?
Which characters are active?
Which characters have Character Bibles?
Which characters have Character History documents?
Which characters are planned?
Which characters are retired?

Character Categories

Natural One Society characters may be organized into the following categories:

Active Characters

Characters currently participating in the project.

Planned Characters

Characters under consideration or development.

Retired Characters

Characters no longer actively developed but preserved for historical reference.

Experimental Characters

Characters being explored through testing and development.

Registry Contents

Registry Usage

The Character Registry should be updated whenever:

A Character Bible is approved.
A character changes status.
A character is retired.

The Character Registry serves as the primary navigation document for character discovery.

Use the Character Registry to locate Character History documents and Character Bibles.

Character History preserves development.

Character Bibles establish authority.

End of Document

I intentionally did not use a table.

looks nice at first, but becomes annoying as the repository grows.

### Healer
Status
History
Bible

is easy to edit, easy to read in GitHub, and easy for future Quill to parse.

--- USER ---
saved. before review I have a question - it is more of an overaching questions about updating the git repo. When we make new characters, remove them, start developing or brainstorming changes to existing characters, etc. How hard will it be to change all these documents and workflows we are creating? It seems like a ton of documents will need changed for each adjustment we make during the creative process

--- CHATGPT ---
That concern is valid — and it means we should design the repo so not every creative thought triggers five document updates.

The rule should be:

Brainstorming changes only the Vault.
Approved canon changes update Canon + Registry.

So during creative development:

Brainstorming / testing
→ Vault only

Strong idea worth preserving
→ Character History

Approved character change
→ Character Bible + Character Registry if status changed

Approved visual change
→ Asset files + Character Bible + Canon Registry if needed

New character approved into project
→ Character Registry + Character folder + optional Character History

You should not update every README every time. READMEs are mostly infrastructure. Once created, they change rarely.

The documents we’re building fall into two categories:

Stable infrastructure:
- Root README
- Vault README
- Character-History README
- QUILL.SYS
- Operating Procedures

Living indexes:
- Character Registry
- Canon Registry

Living canon:
- Character Bibles
- Style Bible
- Asset folders

Most normal creative work will only touch one or two files.

Example: you brainstorm a new Dwarf trait.

Update:
Vault/Character-History/Dwarf.md

Do not update:
README
Vault README
Operating Procedures
Canon Registry
Dwarf Bible

Example: you approve that trait as canon.

Update:
Characters/Dwarf/Bible/Dwarf-Character-Bible...
Canon Registry, only if status/document list changes
Character Registry, only if status changes

So no — this should not become a ton of maintenance. The goal of the structure is to make updates targeted, not heavier.

I would add one simple future rule to Operating Procedures someday:

Do not update infrastructure documents for ordinary creative changes.
Update only the lowest appropriate source of truth.

That protects you from documentation fatigue.

Agreed, but before prompt lib. I have a project question. Right now our characters are not named consistently. Until they have actual names.. is that ok? We have Healer (class) Bard (Class) Orc (Race) Kinder (Race), and Dwarf(race)

--- CHATGPT ---
Yes. I actually think it's completely okay right now.

The key question is:

Are these names identifiers
or
are these names character names?

At the moment, they're identifiers.

Right now:

Orc
Kinder
Dwarf
Healer
Bard

really mean:

The Orc Character

The Kinder Character

The Dwarf Character

The Healer Character

The Bard Character

Those are project labels.

Not necessarily in-universe names.

Why I Would Not Rush To Rename

Suppose tomorrow:

Healer

becomes:

Elyra

If every file is named:

Healer.md
Healer Bible.md
Healer Assets

you can still easily track the evolution.

But if we start renaming files every time a character gets a better name:

Healer
→ Elyra
→ Lady Elyra
→ Elyra the White

the repository becomes harder to navigate.

What I Usually Prefer

Keep the stable identifier.

Then inside the character documentation:

Character Identifier: Healer

Current Name: Elyra

or:

Project Identifier: Healer

Canonical Name: TBD

That gives you:

Stable repository structure
+
Flexible story development

Looking At Your Current Characters

We actually have two different naming schemes:

Healer
Bard

are roles/classes.

while

Orc
Kinder
Dwarf

are species/races.

That inconsistency doesn't bother me yet because they're all functioning as placeholders.

When Would I Change It?

I would change it when a character reaches:

Canon Character Bible Approved

At that point you could decide:

Does this character have an actual canonical name?

If yes:

Identifier: Healer

Canonical Name: Elyra

If no:

Keep Healer

My Recommendation

For now:

Leave them exactly as they are.

Do not rename files.

Do not rename registry entries.

Treat them as:

Character Identifiers

not:

Character Names

In fact, this discussion makes me think we may eventually want a field in the Character Registry like:

Character Identifier:
Healer

Canonical Name:
TBD

But that's a future enhancement, not something I'd add today.

So my answer is:

Current State: Acceptable
Repository Change Needed: No
Future Consideration: Yes

The important thing right now is that everyone—including future Quill—knows which character is which. The current identifiers accomplish that just fine. 📚💾🎲

Prompt Library

Natural One Society Prompt Library

Status: Active

Version: 1.0

Purpose

The Prompt Library preserves approved prompts, workflows, templates, and reusable operational procedures.

The Prompt Library exists to reduce repetitive work, improve consistency, and accelerate future sessions.

The Prompt Library is a preservation and workflow resource.

The Prompt Library does not establish canon.

Authority remains with approved Canon documents and Operating Procedures.

The Prompt Library helps answer:

What prompts are commonly used?
What workflows are repeatable?
How should common tasks be performed?
How can future sessions start more efficiently?
How can successful processes be reused?

Prompt Categories

Natural One Society prompts may be organized into the following categories:

Session Prompts

Prompts used to initialize, recover, or continue project work.

Workflow Prompts

Prompts used to perform repeatable project tasks.

Character Development Prompts

Prompts used during character creation and refinement.

Canon Management Prompts

Prompts used to review, validate, and maintain canon.

Repository Management Prompts

Prompts used to manage repository structure, documentation, and preservation.

Prompt Library Usage

Prompts should be added when they demonstrate consistent value and are likely to be reused.

Experimental prompts may be tested before inclusion.

Approved prompts should be documented clearly enough that future sessions can execute the workflow without requiring historical chat access.

The Prompt Library preserves successful workflows.

The Prompt Library does not replace Operating Procedures.

Navigation

Use the Prompt Library when reing:

Startup procedures
Session recovery
Character development workflows
Canon review workflows
Repository workflows
Reusable operational processes

The Prompt Library should be consulted when a task has been performed successfully before and may benefit from standardization.

Core Philosophy

Reusable knowledge should be preserved.

Successful workflows should be documented.

Repeated tasks should be simplified.

The goal is not to automate creativity.

The goal is to eliminate unnecessary repetition.

The Prompt Library preserves operational knowledge.

End of Document

Save it, read it once, and then we'll perform the same 5-step approval review we've used for every major document so far. 📚💾🎲

Design Decisions

Natural One Society Design Decisions Archive

Status: Active

Version: 1.0

Purpose

The Design Decisions archive preserves the reasoning behind significant project decisions.

The purpose of Design Decisions is to document why important choices were made, what alternatives were considered, and what reasoning led to the final outcome.

The Design Decisions archive is a historical resource.

The Design Decisions archive does not establish canon.

Authority remains with approved Canon documents and Operating Procedures.

The Design Decisions archive helps answer:

Why was a decision made?
What alternatives were considered?
What problems were being solved?
What tradeoffs were evaluated?
What reasoning led to the final outcome?

Decision Categories

Natural One Society design decisions may include:

Repository Decisions

Repository structure, organization, navigation, and preservation systems.

Workflow Decisions

Process design, governance procedures, and operational workflows.

Canon Decisions

Decisions affecting canon structure, organization, and management.

Character Development Decisions

Decisions affecting character creation, development, and documentation.

Asset Management Decisions

Decisions affecting visual assets, authority hierarchy, and asset organization.

Design Decision Usage

Design Decisions should be created when:

A significant project decision is made.
Multiple alternatives are considered.
A decision may require future explanation.
A decision affects repository structure.
A decision affects project workflow.
A decision establishes a new standard or practice.

Design Decisions preserve reasoning.

Design Decisions do not establish authority.

Approved authority remains within Canon documents and Operating Procedures.

Navigation

Use Design Decisions when reing:

Why a process exists
Why a workflow was adopted
Why repository structures were created
Why standards were established
Why alternative approaches were rejected

The Design Decisions archive should be consulted when understanding the reasoning behind important project choices.

Core Philosophy

Decisions should be understandable.

Reasoning should be preserved.

Future contributors should not be required to rediscover solved problems.

The goal is not merely to preserve outcomes.

The goal is to preserve understanding.

The Design Decisions archive preserves project reasoning.

End of Document

This document is slightly different from the others.

Vault README preserves:

History

Character History preserves:

Character evolution

Prompt Library preserves:

Reusable workflows

Design Decisions preserves:

Reasoning

And I think reasoning is one of the easiest things to lose over time.

Save it, review it, and then we'll do the formal approval process. 📚💾🎲
